<p />
<h2><a name="Scope"> Scope </a></h2>
<p />
This document covers installation of the TWiki -1-Feb-2003 production release in the following environment - if you want to use a different environment, feel free to use this as a guideline only.
<p />
<table border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="1"> <tr><th bgcolor="#99CCCC"> <strong>Component</strong> </th><th bgcolor="#99CCCC"> <strong>Name, version</strong> </th><th bgcolor="#99CCCC"> <strong>Comment</strong> </th></tr>
<tr><td>  Operating System  </td><td>  Windows 2000  </td><td>  Should also work for Windows NT  </td></tr>
<tr><td>  Web Server  </td><td>  Apache 1.3.26  </td><td>  Windows-specific security holes fixed in this build <br />(check latest version at <a href="http://httpd.apache.org" target="_top">http://httpd.apache.org</a>, but <strong>don't</strong> use Apache 2.0 yet)  </td></tr>
<tr><td>  Unix tools  </td><td>  Cygwin 1.3.9  </td><td>  Simplest way to get a whole set of required tools  </td></tr>
<tr><td>  Perl </td><td>  Cygwin perl-5.6.1-2  </td><td>  Comes with Cygwin  </td></tr>
<tr><td>  RCS  </td><td>  Cygwin rcs-5.7-2  </td><td>  Comes with Cygwin, includes a file corruption bugfix  </td></tr>
</table>
<p />
Why this choice of packages?  Because I've tried them, and they work well, without requiring a complicated setup... In particular, Apache is the commonest choice for TWiki on Unix/Linux, Cygwin Perl is very close to Unix Perl, and the Cygwin RCS is regularly updated, with a recent TWiki-relevant bug fix in Feb 2002.   Cygwin also lets you install the Unix tools, Perl and RCS in a single step, saving quite a lot of time.
<p />
More recent minor versions should be OK, but they can introduce bugs.  
<p />
<img src="http://192.168.1.49/twiki/pub/TWiki/TWikiDocGraphics/new.gif" border="0" alt="NEW" width="28" height="8" /> Major version upgrades, such as Apache 2.0 and Perl 5.8, are very likely to cause problems - for example, Apache 2.0 is unable to authenticate (see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Support.FailedAuthenticationWithApache2OnWinNT" title="'Support.FailedAuthenticationWithApache2OnWinNT' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Support.FailedAuthenticationWithApache2OnWinNT</a>) users created by the current TWiki user registration script (due to a feature being removed in 2.0), and Perl 5.8 may introduce issues due to its Unicode features.  Even though the Apache group says that Apache 2.0 is the best version, that's not true for TWiki.
<p />
<h3><a name="Alternatives"> Alternatives  </a></h3>
<p />
There are doubtless other combinations of components that may work - in particular:
<p />
<ul>
<li> <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActiveState" title="'Codev.ActiveState' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActiveState</a> Perl involves only minor changes to <code>TWiki.cfg</code>, and is probably a simpler choice if you need an easy way to install mod_perl (see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ModPerl" title="'Codev.ModPerl' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ModPerl</a>).  <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActiveState" title="'Codev.ActiveState' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActiveState</a> Perl can be substituted without too much hassle, and in fact the same <code>TWiki.cfg</code> can be used for both <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActiveState" title="'Codev.ActiveState' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActiveState</a> and Cygwin Perl.  
</li>
<li> Using a different web server is certainly possible, but the setup required for each webserver varies greatly (see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.TWikiOnWindows" title="'Codev.TWikiOnWindows' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.TWikiOnWindows</a> for pages about specific web servers).  You may find it easiest to get a working system with Apache and then switch over to another web server.
</li>
<li> Windows NT works fine.
</li>
<li> Windows XP should work in theory, but see the Apache site for details of XP-related bugs, and other packages' sites for any peculiarities of XP.  Please report any XP installations on <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.TWikiOnWindowsKnownConfigurations" title="'Codev.TWikiOnWindowsKnownConfigurations' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.TWikiOnWindowsKnownConfigurations</a>, and comment at <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments" title="'Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments</a>.
</li>
<li> Windows 98 is reported to work for at least one person - see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Support.TwikiOnWindowsBinaryAttachments" title="'Support.TwikiOnWindowsBinaryAttachments' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Support.TwikiOnWindowsBinaryAttachments</a>.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
Covering the whole range of additional possibilities, particularly web servers, would make this cookbook too complex, and is best handled as a separate activity.
<p />
<h2><a name="Checking_versions"> Checking versions </a></h2>
<p />
If you already have some of these add-ons installed, here's how to check the versions - this assumes you have <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CygWin" title="'Codev.CygWin' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CygWin</a> already installed:
<p />
<pre>
   $ <i>: Cygwin DLL version is the number in 1.3.x format</i>
   $ uname -r
   $ less c:/<i>your-apache-dir</i>/Announcement
   $ perl -v
   $ rcs -V
</pre>
<p />
<p />
If you have an older version of any component, do yourself a favour and <strong>upgrade it</strong> as part of the install process.
<p />
<h2><a name="Pre_requisites_and_upgrades"> Pre-requisites and upgrades </a></h2>
<p />
You will need to have local administrator rights and to be comfortable with Windows administration.
<p />
This cookbook is intended for a clean install, i.e. none of these components are already installed.  However, since Cygwin and Apache's installation process is fairly upgrade-friendly, upgrades should work as well - take backups of all your data and config files first, though!
<p />
<h3><a name="Text_editing"> Text editing </a></h3>
<p />
Editing Cygwin files is best done with an editor that can handle Unix file format (see the Cygwin binary mode section below) - the installation process includes <code>nano</code>, a non-GUI editor, but if you prefer to use a GUI editor, you should first install PFE, a freeware editor that supports Unix format files.  PFE is available on <a href="http://download.cnet.com/downloads/0-4003619-100-904159.html?tag=st.dl.10001-103-1.lst-7-1.904159" target="_top">download.com</a> and <a href="http://www.simtel.net/pub/dl/11983.shtml" target="_top">Simtel</a>.
<p />
Another good <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.OpenSource" title="'Codev.OpenSource' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.OpenSource</a> editor is SciTE (aka WSciTE), available at <a href="http://www.scintilla.org/SciTE.html" target="_top">http://www.scintilla.org/SciTE.html</a>.
<p />
<h2><a name="The_Unix_Windows_Environment"> The Unix/Windows Environment </a></h2>
<p />
It's a little known fact that you can use pathnames such as <code><b>c:/apache</b></code> almost everywhere in Windows - try it in a File Open dialogue box.  The main exception is the Win2000 <code>cmd.exe</code> command line shell - here, you must use double quotes around forward slashes, e.g. <code>dir "c:/apache"</code> will work fine.
<p />
The reason this matters is that <code><b>'\'</b></code> is a special character to Perl and other tools, so it's much easier to use <code><b>'/'</b></code> everywhere.  
<p />
<h3><a name="The_Cygwin_environment"> The Cygwin environment </a></h3>
<p />
<a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CygWin" title="'Codev.CygWin' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CygWin</a> is a Unix-like environment for Windows - many of its tools support the <code>c:/apache</code> format, but it also provides a more Unixlike syntax, e.g. <code>/usr/bin/rcs.exe</code>, because some Unix tools ported onto Cygwin only support the Unix format.
<p />
When you launch a Cygwin shell, your existing PATH variable is translated from the Windows format to the Unix format, and the ';' separators in the Windows PATH are changed into ':' separators as required by Unix.  A Cygwin tool (e.g. Cygwin Perl or Cygwin RCS) will always use the Unix PATH format, and will accept Unix format pathnames.
<p />
<h3><a name="The_Apache_environment"> The Apache environment </a></h3>
<p />
Apache runs as a native Windows process and has nothing to do with Cygwin (at least the version used in this cookbook doesn't).  Hence it supports c:/ pathnames in its config files and the first line of Perl CGI scripts.
<p />
If you need to use spaces in file names (not recommended), put double quotes around the file name in the <code>httpd.conf</code> file. There have been some security-related bugs in Apache with long pathnames, which are a bit more likely if you use spaces, so it's best to just avoid long names and using spaces.
<p />
<h3><a name="The_Perl_environment"> The Perl environment </a></h3>
<p />
Once Perl has been launched by Apache, it is in Cygwin mode, and so is everything it launches, including <code>ls</code>, <code>egrep</code>, and RCS tools that it (typically) launches with the <code>bash</code> shell.
<p />
If you need to use spaces in file names (not recommended), you <em>may</em> be able to put double quotes around the file name in the <code>TWiki.cfg</code> file - however, it's not clear whether all the TWiki code would work with this.
<p />
<p />
<h2><a name="Installing_Components"> Installing Components </a></h2>
<p />
Enough background, let's get on with the installation.
<p />
<h3><a name="TWiki_part_1_"> TWiki (part 1) </a></h3>
<p />
Head to <a href="http://twiki.org" target="_top">http://twiki.org</a>, click the download link, and fill in the form to request a URL for download. You'll get an automated email, which should arrive by the time you need it.
<p />
<h3><a name="Apache"> Apache </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>1. Download Apache</strong>
<ul>
<li> Check at <a href="http://httpd.apache.org/" target="_top">http://httpd.apache.org/</a> for any security announcements
</li>
<li> Check the latest 1.3.x version number on <a href="http://www.apache.org/dist/httpd/Announcement.html" target="_top">this page</a>
</li>
<li> Find a local mirror using <a href="http://www.apache.org/dyn/closer.cgi" target="_top">http://www.apache.org/dyn/closer.cgi</a> - choose httpd, then binaries, then win32
</li>
<li> The file to download is <code><b>apache_1.3.X-win32-x86-no_src.msi</b></code> where 'X' is 20 or higher 
<ul>
<li> Note that this is a Microsoft Installer format file (.MSI) - this is supported by Windows 2000.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: If you are using Windows NT, download the .MSI installer (<code><b>instmsi.exe</b></code>) from the <a href="http://httpd.apache.org/dist/httpd/binaries/win32/" target="_top">Apache Win32 download page</a> - this enables you to install .MSI files.  You may need to update the .MSI Installer if you have an old version under NT.
</li>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: The Apache package itself requires a download of around 2 MB, and up to 10 MB of free disk space once installed.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<strong>2. Install Apache</strong>
<ul>
<li> Double-click the .MSI file to run the installer
</li>
<li> Specify <code><b>c:\</b></code> as the installation directory - this actually installs Apache into <code><b>c:\apache</b></code> (if you specify <code>c:\apache</code>, it installs into <code>c:\apache\Apache</code>).  <em>Putting Apache into <code>c:\Program Files</code> is not recommended for easy editing of Apache config files from Cygwin.</em>  
</li>
<li> You can choose to run Apache as a Win2000 service or as a normal program - see the Apache docs for details.  
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: Needs a bit more detail here... See the excellent documents about <a href="http://httpd.apache.org/docs/windows.html" target="_top">Installing Apache on Windows</a> and <a href="http://httpd.apache.org/docs/win_service.html" target="_top">Running Apache as a Windows NT/2000 service</a>.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<strong>3. Test Apache</strong>
<ul>
<li> If necessary, start apache, either as a Win2000 service (using Admin Tools | Computer Management, or by typing <code>apache -k start -n apache</code>) or standalone (by typing <code>apache -k start</code>)
</li>
<li> Point your browser at <a href="http://yourdomain.com/" target="_top">http://yourdomain.com/</a> to see the Apache intro page.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
Congratulations, you now have a working web server! 
<p />
To restart Apache after changing its config, type:
<p />
<ul>
<li> <code>apache -k restart</code> for standalone Apache process running in another window
</li>
<li> <code>apache -k restart -n apache</code> for Apache running as a Win2000 service (-n gives name of service)
</li>
</ul>
<p />
Another useful command is <code>apache -k stop</code>.
<p />
<h3><a name="Cygwin_Unix_tools_Perl_and_RCS"> </a> Cygwin, Unix tools, Perl and RCS </h3>
<p />
<strong>4. Install Cygwin</strong>
<p />
Head to <a href="http://cygwin.com" target="_top">http://cygwin.com</a>, and click the <strong><em>Install Cygwin Now</em></strong> link.  Save the <code>setup.exe</code> in a directory, e.g.  <code>c:\download\cygwin-dist</code>. 
<p />
Now run the Cygwin <code>setup.exe</code> file - this will also install Perl and RCS in one fell swoop.
<ul>
<li> Choose Internet install
</li>
<li> On first page, accept the defaults (be sure that the <strong><em>default text file type is Unix</em></strong> to avoid problems with attachment uploads, and specify 'install for all users')
</li>
<li> Select <code>c:\download\cygwin-dist</code> as the local package directory, and suitable proxy settings, then pick a local mirror site
</li>
<li> In the package list screen, hit the <strong>View</strong> button until you get an alphabetical list that says <strong>Full</strong> to the right of the button.
</li>
<li> Leave the radio button on <strong>Curr</strong> (Current)
<ul>
<li> The Current column shows what's installed on your system (if anything)
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> For each package, make sure the <strong>New</strong> column in the installer has a version number under it. If it says 'Skip' or 'Keep' (meaning it's already installed), single-click that word until a version number is shown.  Make sure you select the following packages:
<ul>
<li> <code>bash</code>
</li>
<li> <code>binutils</code>
</li>
<li> <code>diffutils</code>
</li>
<li> <code>gcc</code>
</li>
<li> <code>grep</code>
</li>
<li> <code>gzip</code>
</li>
<li> <code>make</code>
</li>
<li> <code>nano</code>
</li>
<li> <code>ncftp</code>
</li>
<li> <code>pcre</code>
</li>
<li> <code>perl</code> (5.6.1-2 or higher)
</li>
<li> <code>rcs</code>  (5.7-2 or higher)
</li>
<li> <code>tar</code>
</li>
<li> <code>textutils</code>
</li>
<li> <code>unzip</code>
</li>
<li> <code>w32api</code>
</li>
<li> <code>wget</code> (optional, useful for Perl install and <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ReadWriteOfflineWiki" title="'Codev.ReadWriteOfflineWiki' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ReadWriteOfflineWiki</a>)
</li>
<li> NOTE: Do <strong>not</strong> include <code>lynx</code> if you are upgrading from an older Cygwin installation (to avoid annoying DLL messages) - if you want Lynx, read the <a href="http://cygwin.com/faq/faq.html#SEC32" target="_top">Cygwin FAQ entry</a> and upgrade <code>libncurses5</code>.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Hit Next to do the installation.  
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: The mandatory packages require a download of about 12 MB - about half of this is Perl, which would be necessary even without Cygwin, and most of the rest is <code>gcc</code>, which is required for simple installation of Perl modules that use the C language.  Something like 20 to 30 MB of free disk space should be enough for Cygwin, but I didn't test this (try a <code>du -k /</code> after a new install and let me know the last figure).
</li>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: The installer keeps a local copy of downloaded files, so it's easy to re-install without re-downloading.  
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Let the installer create the shortcuts suggested
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<strong>5. Test Cygwin</strong>
<ul>
<li> Launch the desktop icon - this runs the <code>bash</code> shell, which has command line editing features
<ul>
<li> Use the cursor up key to recall previous commands - normal PC editing keys can then be used to edit a command
</li>
<li> TIP: When typing a directory or file name, hit the TAB key after the first few letters of the name - <code>bash</code> will 'complete' the name.  If <code>bash</code> beeps at you, hit TAB again to see the files/directories that match the name so far, and type a bit more before hitting TAB.  This saves a lot of time!
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Type <code>rcs -V</code> - you should see the RCS version, 5.7
</li>
<li> Type <code>perl -v</code> - you should see cygwin mentioned in the first line, and the Perl version, 5.6.1
</li>
<li> Type <code>grep home /etc/passwd</code> - you should see some output.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
The <a href="http://cygwin.com/cygwin-ug-net/cygwin-ug-net.html" target="_top">Cygwin User Guide</a> is well worth reading for some background on how Cygwin works.
<p />
<strong>6. Configure Cygwin for binary mode</strong>
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>This is very important - omitting this step leads to a partially working system that corrupts RCS files</em></strong> - without this, Cygwin tools (including Perl and RCS) will add unwanted carriage returns (Ctrl/M, '\r') to files in an attempt to translate between the Windows and Unix text file formats (Unix text files only use line feeds ('\n').
<ul>
<li> This has been a great time sink, causing numerous subtle problems - see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CookbookLineEndingProblems" title="'Codev.CookbookLineEndingProblems' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CookbookLineEndingProblems</a>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Stay in the Cygwin (bash) shell, and type the following (use only forward slashes, i.e. '/'):
</li>
</ul>
<pre>
   $ <b>mkdir /twiki /c c:/twiki</b>
   $ <b>mount -b -s c:/twiki /twiki</b>
   $ <b>mount -b -s c:/ /c</b>
   $ <b>mount -b -c /cygdrive</b>
   $ <b>mount</b>
   Device              Directory           Type         Flags
   C:\cygwin\bin       /usr/bin            system       binmode
   C:\cygwin\lib       /usr/lib            system       binmode
   C:\cygwin           /                   system       binmode
   c:\twiki            /twiki              system       binmode
   c:                  /c                  system       binmode
</pre>
<ul>
<li> This configures <code>/twiki</code> (known as a 'mount point') to map onto <code>c:/twiki</code> and for that directory tree to always be in binary mode, and does the same for <code>/c</code>, mapping it onto <code>c:/</code>. The last-but-one command sets binary as the default for any unmounted drives (e.g. <code>z:/</code>, aka <code>/cygdrive/z</code>).
</li>
<li> It is <strong>very important</strong> that all lines in the output of <code>mount</code> say 'binmode' under Flags
<ul>
<li> If the lines for <code>C:\cygwin</code> directories do not, you should uninstall and then re-install Cygwin to ensure that binary attachment uploads will work.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> You can now refer to files using Unix paths, e.g. <code>/twiki/bin/view</code> or <code>/c/apache/Announcement</code> - see the <a href="http://www.cygwin.com/cygwin-ug-net/using.html" target="_top">Cygwin documentation</a> for more details on this.
</li>
<li> Now test this, still using the Cygwin shell:
<ul>
<li> Type <code><b>cd /twiki</b></code>
</li>
<li> Type <code><b>echo hi &gt;t</b></code> 
</li>
<li> Type <code><b>cat -v t</b></code> - you should see <code><b>hi</b></code> as the output
</li>
<li> If you see filename errors, your <strong>mounts did not work</strong> for some reason - check your typing
</li>
<li> If you see <code><b>hi^M</b></code> as output, <strong>your /twiki directory is not in binary mode</strong>
</li>
<li> Clean up by doing <code>rm t</code>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
This setup is written to the Windows registry, so there's no need to put these commands into a <code>.profile</code> file.  For more information on binary vs text mode, see this <a href="http://cygwin.com/cygwin-ug-net/using-textbinary.html" target="_top">User Guide section</a> and this <a href="http://cygwin.com/faq/faq.html#SEC54" target="_top">FAQ entry</a>.
<p />
<h3><a name="TWiki_part_2_"> TWiki (part 2) </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>7. Download TWiki</strong>
<p />
Download the latest TWiki release from the URL that <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> sent you, and save it in the <code>c:/twiki</code> directory.
<p />
<strong>8. Install TWiki</strong>
<p />
Unzip the ZIP file under <code>c:/twiki</code> using <a href="http://www.winzip.com/" target="_top">WinZip</a>, or by going into Cygwin and doing the following - you can hit the <code>TAB</code> key to complete filenames after you've typed the first part:
<pre>
   $ <b>cd /twiki</b>
   $ <b>unzip TWiki20011201.zip</b>
</pre>
<p />
<h2><a name="Configuring_components"> Configuring components </a></h2>
<p />
Now that all the components are installed, you need to configure them.
<p />
<h3><a name="Configuring_Apache"> Configuring Apache </a></h3>
<p />
The setup given here is fairly simple, in that it allows only TWiki to be served by the web server.  For more complex setups, you can investigate the Alias and ScriptAlias commands that are left commented out in this configuration. 
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: This needs reviewing for security holes and to ensure nothing is missed, though this config does work.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<strong>1. Configure Apache (part 1)</strong>
<p />
Using a suitable text editor (e.g. Cygwin's <code>'nano'</code>, or the Windows <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiDocumentation#Text_editing">PFE editor</a>, unless you already know <code>'vi'</code>), edit <code>c:/apache/conf/httpd.conf</code> as follows - this tells Apache where TWiki lives, and removes the need to tinker with the Windows 2000 environment settings.
<ul>
<li> If you are using nano, <strong>always</strong> launch it with <code>nano -w filename</code> - this turns off wrapping of long lines.
</li>
<li> Note the trailing '/' characters in various places - they are important!
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> Create the <code>c:\temp</code> directory, by typing <code>mkdir c:\temp</code> in a DOS command line window
</li>
<li> Edit the following lines, some of which already exist in the file:
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
# Change this to point to the Apache administrator (e.g. you)
ServerAdmin you@yourdomain.com

# Replaces DocumentRoot "C:/apache/htdocs"
DocumentRoot "C:/twiki"

# Replaces &lt;Directory "C:/apache/htdocs">
&lt;Directory "C:/twiki">

</pre>
<p />
<ul>
<li> Add the following lines - the Alias and ScriptAlias lines can be omitted in this setup
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
# Alias /twiki/ "C:/twiki/"
# ScriptAlias /twiki/bin/ "C:/twiki/bin/"
&lt;Directory  "C:/twiki/bin/">
    # RD: Changed None to All in next line, to enable .htaccess
    AllowOverride All
    Allow From All
    Options  ExecCGI
    SetHandler cgi-script
&lt;/Directory>

# Environment setup required to run Apache as service or as a
# standalone process.
&lt;IfModule mod_env.c>
   # Adjust TZ for your server timezone, e.g. EST5EDT - put the non-daylight-savings
   # timezone code first (e.g. EST or GMT), followed by the number of hours that it's behind GMT 
   # during non-daylight-savings time (use '-5' for timezones in advance of GMT).
   SetEnv TZ GMT0BST
   SetEnv RCSINIT -x,v/
   # Adjust TEMP and TMP for your server and create directories if necessary
   SetEnv TEMP c:/temp
   SetEnv TMP c:/temp
   SetEnv LOGNAME system
   SetEnv HOME c:/twiki
&lt;/IfModule>
</pre>
<p />
<strong>2. Configure Apache (part 2)</strong>
<p />
Add an AddHandler line to the <code><b>&lt;IfModule mod_mime.c&gt;</b></code> section of <code>httpd.conf</code> - this removes the need to rename all the TWiki CGI scripts later in the installation.  
<ul>
<li> Note the trailing '.' on the AddHandler line.
</li>
</ul>
<pre>
#
# Document types
#
&lt;IfModule mod_mime.c>
    # TWiki setup - avoid renaming scripts
    <b>AddHandler cgi-script .</b>
&lt;/IfModule>
</pre>
<p />
<h3><a name="Configuring_TWiki"> Configuring TWiki </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>3. Configure TWiki</strong>
<p />
Edit the TWiki config file, <code>c:/twiki/lib/TWiki.cfg</code> (or in Cygwin terms, <code>/twiki/lib/TWiki.cfg</code>) as follows:
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: It should be possible to use <code>c:/twiki</code> format pathnames for Cygwin, given the above binmode setup, but I have not tested this fully - a Cygwin Perl test script does generate binary mode files in this configuration, so it should work with RCS as well (really need a small RCS file corruption test case).  Watch out for RCS file corruption carefully if you do try <code>c:/twiki</code> pathnames with Cygwin, and do report your experiences... 
</li>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: Some recent versions of Cygwin (e.g. 1.3.10) seem to create 'symbolic links' from <code>fgrep</code> and <code>egrep</code> to <code>grep</code>, requiring the settings for these commands to point directly to <code>grep</code> (with suitable flags to provide <code>fgrep</code> and <code>egrep</code> behaviour).
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
# variables that need to be changed when installing on a new server:
# ==================================================================
#                   http://your.domain.com/twiki : link of TWiki icon in upper left corner :
$wikiHomeUrl      = <b>"http://yourdomain.com/bin/view"</b>;
#                   Host of TWiki URL :    (Example "http://myhost.com:123")
$defaultUrlHost   = <b>"http://yourdomain.com"</b>;
#                   /twiki/bin : cgi-bin path of TWiki URL:
$scriptUrlPath    = <b>"/bin"</b>;
#                   /twiki/pub : Public data path of TWiki URL (root of attachments) :
$pubUrlPath       = <b>"/pub"</b>;

# NOTE: Next three settings should be valid absolute pathnames using Cygwin; if using
# TWiki:Codev.ActiveState Perl, use z:/twiki format pathnames if your TWiki directory is not on C:.

#                   Public data directory, must match $pubUrlPath :
$pubDir           = <b>"/twiki/pub"</b>;
#                   Template directory :
$templateDir      = <b>"/twiki/templates"</b>;
#                   Data (topic files) root directory :
$dataDir          = <b>"/twiki/data"</b>;

....

#                   Set ENV{'PATH'} explicitly for taint checks ( #!perl -T option ) :
#                   (Note: PATH environment variable is not changed if set to "")

# On Windows, $safeEnvPath needs only one component, the directory where RCS is installed
# - used by 'rcsdiff' to run 'co' program, so PATH must be correct.

# Unix/Linux setting:
# $safeEnvPath      = "/bin:/usr/bin";

# Using Cygwin perl, so can use Unix-like paths, with ':' as separator.
# Note that /usr/bin and /bin are identical due to default /usr/bin mount
# in Cygwin.  Must NOT use 'c:/foo' type paths, as ':' is taken as separator
# meaning that 'c' is interpreted as a pathname, giving Perl taint error.
$safeEnvPath      = <b>"/bin"</b>;

# If using ActiveState perl, use Windows paths instead
# $safeEnvPath      = "c:/cygwin/bin";

...

#                   RCS directory (find out by 'which rcs') :
$rcsDir           = <b>"c:/cygwin/bin"</b>;

...

#                   Unix egrep command :
$egrepCmd         = <b>"/bin/grep -E"</b>;
#                   Unix fgrep command :
$fgrepCmd         = <b>"/bin/grep -F"</b>;
</pre>
<p />
For the cookbook install using Cygwin Perl, there's no more <code>TWiki.cfg</code> editing to be done, so you can get onto the next section.  
<p />
<ul>
<li> For <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActiveState" title="'Codev.ActiveState' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActiveState</a> Perl, you need to make these additional edits further down the file - this is the only place where backslashes are needed.  (See <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CookbookActivePerlSetup" title="'Codev.CookbookActivePerlSetup' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CookbookActivePerlSetup</a> for some extra Perl setup that should remove the need for these edits.)
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
#                   NOTE: When using ActiveState Perl, you must specify
#                   a full Windows-style pathname, using '\\' for backslashes,
#                   for the ls, egrep and fgrep commands, because Cygwin's shell
#                   is not used - forward slashes are OK in Windows everywhere
#                   except in the cmd.exe shell. Drive letters are OK - e.g.
#                   'c:\\foo\\ls' will work.  When using Cygwin perl, just
#                   use the default '/bin/ls' type settings.
#
#                   Unix ls command :
$lsCmd            = "c:\\cygwin\\bin\\ls";
#                   Unix egrep command :
$egrepCmd         = "c:\\cygwin\\bin\\grep";
#                   Unix fgrep command :
$fgrepCmd         = "c:\\cygwin\\bin\\grep";
</pre>
<p />
<p />
<p />
<h2><a name="Editing_the_CGI_scripts"> </a> Editing the CGI scripts </h2>
<p />
<strong>4. Editing the Shebang lines</strong>
<p />
Now to edit the curiously named 'shebang lines' at the top of the TWiki CGI scripts...  
<ul>
<li> You <strong>must</strong> use the Cygwin shell to do this (unless you are a Perl expert) - <strong>don't use</strong> the Windows command shell, cmd.exe (aka DOS Prompt)      
</li>
<li> Then do the following, which quickly edits the 19 or so files, using Perl - the important lines are in bold.
</li>
<li> Type the Perl line <strong>very carefully</strong>
<ul>
<li> If you do mis-type the <code><b>perl</b></code> line, you can restore from the <code>.backup</code> directory and re-run the command, as it will only edit the original files, not the backups with '~' suffixes.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
$ <b>cd /twiki/bin</b>

$ ls
attach   geturl         oops     rdiff     save        testenv  viewfile
changes  installpasswd  passwd   register  search      upload
edit     mailnotify     preview  rename    statistics  view

$ <b>mkdir .backup </b>
$ <b>cp * .backup</b>

$ head -1 view
#!/usr/bin/perl -wT

$ <b>perl -pi~ -e 's;#!/usr/bin/perl;#!c:/cygwin/bin/perl;' *[a-z]</b>

$ <b>head -1 view</b>
#!c:/cygwin/bin/perl -wT

$ ls
attach    geturl          oops      rdiff      save         testenv   viewfile~
attach~   geturl~         oops~     rdiff~     save~        testenv~  view~
changes   installpasswd   passwd    register   search       upload
changes~  installpasswd~  passwd~   register~  search~      upload~
edit      mailnotify      preview   rename     statistics   view
edit~     mailnotify~     preview~  rename~    statistics~  viewfile

</pre>
<p />
If for some reason the edit goes wrong, just type <code>cp .backup/* .</code> (while within the <code>bin</code> directory) to restore the original distribution files.  Use <code>ls -a</code> to see the <code>.backup</code> directory, and <code>ls -a .backup</code> to view its contents. 
<p />
Optional step: you can do <code>'rm *~'</code> to clean out the backups made by Perl, but that's not essential as all the original files cannot be executed.  If you do this, <strong>type the command very carefully</strong>, as a space after the '*' will wipe out all files in this directory!
<p />
<strong>5. Minor changes to TWiki scripts</strong>
<p />
As an interlude, you now need to make some minor edits to files in the <code>c:/twiki/bin</code> directory, using a suitable editor (remember to use <code>nano -w filename</code> if you prefer <code>nano</code> to <code>vi</code> - or just use the Windows <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiDocumentation#Pre_requisites_and_upgrades">PFE editor</a>).
<p />
<ul>
<li> Edit the <code>register</code> script in <code>/twiki/bin</code> - change line 200 to read as follows (insert the <code><b>MIME::Base64::</b></code> part):
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
         return $user . ':{SHA}' . <b>MIME::Base64::</b>encode_base64(Digest::SHA1::sha1($passwd));
</pre>
<p />
<ul>
<li> If you are using <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActiveState" title="'Codev.ActiveState' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActiveState</a> Perl, you also need to update <code>testenv</code>, see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CookbookActivePerlTestenv" title="'Codev.CookbookActivePerlTestenv' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CookbookActivePerlTestenv</a>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<h3><a name="Perl_module_installation"> Perl module installation </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>6. Installing required Perl modules</strong>
<p />
Some additional Perl modules are needed for the <code>register</code> script to work properly.  Fortunately, there is an automated tool that makes it easy to do this - it's called <code>cpan</code>, and goes to the Perl module archive site, <a href="http://www.cpan.org/" target="_top">http://www.cpan.org/</a>, to download all required modules, and then build and install them.  Here's what you need to do:
<p />
First of all, you need to get the <code>cpan</code> tool configured and working - this is only necessary once.  From the Cygwin shell, type the following (putting the <code>export</code> command in <code>~/.profile</code> is recommended to make this setting persistent).  Without the TEMP variable, some modules may fail to install on Windows 2000 and higher.
<pre>
$ <b>export TEMP=/c/temp</b>
$ <b>cpan</b>
<i>Lots of questions about configuration and preferences - just hit Enter until you 
get to the questions about mirror sites, but answer the questions about FTP proxies etc
 if you are behind a proxy-based firewall.  The CPAN tool will fetch a series of files, 
some quite large, as part of this setup process, so be patient...</i>

</pre>
<p />
<strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: If you are behind a non-proxy-based firewall that requires the use of passive FTP, the initial downloads of files using Net::FTP may appear to hang - just wait 5 or more minutes, however, and the CPAN tool should eventually hit on <code>ncftpget</code>, which is part of Cygwin and does work OK.  If this doesn't work and you are behind a typical NAT-based firewall, try doing the following at the Cygwin shell before running <code>cpan</code> - this forces Net::FTP to use passive FTP, letting it get through such firewalls:
<pre>
$ <b>export FTP_PASSIVE=1</b>
</pre>
If this works, add this line to your <code>~/.profile</code> file for future use.
<p />
Once some initial files are downloaded, you are asked to select your continent and country, and then mirror sites - just type the number of the mirror sites you want to use (pick a few in case one is down):
<pre>
...
(28) Turkey
(29) Ukraine
(30) United Kingdom

Select your country (or several nearby countries) [] 30

(1) ftp://cpan.teleglobe.net/pub/CPAN
(2) ftp://ftp.clockerz.net/pub/CPAN/
(3) ftp://ftp.demon.co.uk/pub/CPAN/
(4) ftp://ftp.flirble.org/pub/languages/perl/CPAN/
(5) ftp://ftp.mirror.ac.uk/sites/ftp.funet.fi/pub/languages/perl/CPAN/
(6) ftp://ftp.plig.org/pub/CPAN/
(7) ftp://mirror.uklinux.net/pub/CPAN/
(8) ftp://sunsite.doc.ic.ac.uk/packages/CPAN/
(9) ftp://usit.shef.ac.uk/pub/packages/CPAN/
Select as many URLs as you like,
put them on one line, separated by blanks [] 4 7 8

Enter another URL or RETURN to quit: []
New set of picks:
  ftp://ftp.flirble.org/pub/languages/perl/CPAN/
  ftp://mirror.uklinux.net/pub/CPAN/
  ftp://sunsite.doc.ic.ac.uk/packages/CPAN/

</pre>
<p />
Eventually, you'll get to the CPAN tool's shell prompt, where you need to install a few modules - the tool will do all the work for you.  
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: You will need to have previously installed the Cygwin <code>make</code> and <code>gcc</code> packages, which are required by the CPAN installer (<code>gcc</code> is required for modules that include C language code) - you can install them now by launching Cygwin's <code>setup.exe</code> from <code>c:/download/cygwin-dist</code> (no need to exit the CPAN installer).
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<pre>
cpan shell -- CPAN exploration and modules installation (v1.59_54)
cpan> <b>install Net::SMTP</b>
<i>May already be installed - if it is, try 'force install', since it's useful to be able to set
firewall and passive FTP configuration when using Net::FTP.  <b>Make sure you answer 'Y' to the question 
about whether you want to configure this package.</b></i>
cpan> <b>install Digest::SHA1</b>
<i>Lots of output about how CPAN finds, builds and installs the module - watch for 
any errors, though it should work fine if you have installed the Cygwin packages listed above (particularly 'gcc' and 'make').</i>
cpan> <b>install MIME::Base64</b>
<i>May already be installed.</i>

</pre>
<p />
<h3><a name="Re_locking_RCS_files"> </a> Re-locking RCS files </h3>
<p />
<strong>7. Re-locking files</strong>
<p />
First, some testing: in your browser, go to <a href="http://yourdomain.com/bin/testenv" target="_top">http://yourdomain.com/bin/testenv</a> - this provides a lot of detail, including warnings.  Write down the Apache server's userid that is given by this script - typically either 'system' or 'administrator' - I'll assume 'system' from now on.
<ul>
<li> If the <code>testenv</code> script doesn't work, go back and check the configuration of the Apache <code>httpd.conf</code> file, and <code>TWiki.cfg</code>.  Have a look at the Apache error log, <code>c:/apache/logs/error_log</code>, and the TWiki error log, <code>/twiki/data/log*.txt</code>.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
This 'system' user must own the locks on the RCS files, which are shipped with the lock held by 'nobody'.  The reason this matters is that no revisions will be tracked by RCS unless the Apache userid matches that of the RCS file locks.
<p />
You can re-lock files using <code>rcs -u</code> and <code>rcs -l</code>, but it's a painfully manual process.  Instead, just use Perl again to mass-edit all the RCS files, as follows:
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE</em></strong>: The 'NR &lt;= 10' part of the Perl command ensures that it only operates on the first 10 lines, to avoid editing the body of RCS files for topics that happen to include the text 'nobody:' (like this one...)
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<p />
<pre>
$ <b>cd /twiki/data</b>

$ : Make a backup of all files
$ <b>tar czvf all-files.tar.gz */*</b>

$ : Test edit a single file to check your typing
$ <b>perl -pi~~~ -e 'NR <= 10 && s/nobody:/system:/ ' Main/WebIndex.txt,v</b>

$ <b>diff Main/WebIndex.txt,v Main/WebIndex.txt,v~~~</b>
5c5
<       system:1.2; strict;
---
>       nobody:1.2; strict;

$ : Now edit all the RCS files at once - use cursor-up to recall previous command
$ <b>perl -pi~~~ -e 'NR <= 10 && s/nobody:/system:/ ' */*,v</b>

$ : Check for any remaining files not edited
$ <b>grep 'strict;$' */*,v | grep -v system</b>

$ : Clean up - type this <b>very carefully</b> 
$ <b>rm */*~~~</b>
</pre>
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong>If something goes wrong:</strong> to restore your existing files from the backup, just type <code>tar xzvf all-files.tar.gz</code> and all your files, both .txt and .txt,v, will be back as they were before the edits.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
You have now re-locked all the RCS files and are almost ready to start using TWiki!  
<p />
<h3><a name="Email_setup"> Email setup </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>8. Email setup for notification and registration</strong>
<p />
You need to set the <code>SMTPMAILHOST</code> to an SMTP email host that is reachable and currently working.  Otherwise you'll get a confusing message from TWiki when registering new users or running <code>mailnotify</code> (for <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebNotify">WebNotify</a>), along the lines of:
<p />
<pre>
   Software Error: Can't call method "mail" on an undefined value at ../lib/TWiki/Net.pm line 187.
</pre>
<p />
There are other settings to be made in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a>, e.g. the <code>WIKIWEBMASTER</code> and (probably) the <code>SMTPSENDERHOST</code> (normally your mail server or TWiki server).  See the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a> for more details, what's listed here is just enough to let you run the basic tests.
<p />
<h2><a name="Testing_your_TWiki_installation"> Testing your TWiki installation </a></h2>
<p />
It is important to test your TWiki installation before you release it to other users or put any significant data into it.
<p />
Here are the main things to test:
<p />
<ul>
<li> testenv - use <code>http://yourdomain.com/bin/testenv</code> and check for warnings
</li>
<li> Page viewing (<code>view</code> script) - click around a few pages and make sure the links are OK
</li>
<li> RCS diffs (<code>rdiff</code> script) - click on the Diffs link and on the '&gt;' links at bottom of page
</li>
<li> Edit a page, and register as a new user - tests page creation, use of <code>register</code> script to create a new user entry in <code>/twiki/data/.htpasswd</code> (the Apache password file), ability to send email via Net::SMTP, and whether <code>SMTPMAILHOST</code> was set correctly in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a>.
<ul>
<li> If you get a failure to register or send email, check the Apache error log, and that all CPAN modules were installed correctly in Step 6, <em>Installing required Perl modules</em>.
</li>
<li> Try typing <code>tail -30 /c/apache/logs/error_log</code> to see last 30 errors from Apache
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Edit a page - check revision increased and set to current date/time
</li>
<li> Edit the same page using another browser or PC, logging in as a different user - check there's a lock message (which you can override) and no double lines
</li>
<li> Check the Apache <code>error_log</code> file to see if there are any RCS errors so far
</li>
<li> Index - tests whether <code>ls</code> and <code>grep</code> are working
</li>
<li> Search - more tests for whether <code>ls</code> and <code>grep</code> are working
</li>
<li> Attachments - tests access to <code>/twiki/pub</code> directory.
<ul>
<li> Try a binary attachment upload and check the number of bytes in the file has not changed - if it has, see the <strong>Install Cygwin</strong> section's note on the default text file type.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Check the Apache <code>error_log</code> file again
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<h3><a name="Troubleshooting"> Troubleshooting  </a></h3>
<p />
If anything doesn't work, go back and check the configuration of the Apache <code>httpd.conf</code> file, and <code>TWiki.cfg</code>.  Have a look at the Apache error log, <code>c:/apache/logs/error_log</code>, and the TWiki error log, <code>/twiki/data/log*.txt</code>, and if necessary enable debugging on selected scripts (the commands are right at the top of each script) - the results go into <code>/twiki/data/debug.txt</code>.  There is also a <code>/twiki/data/warning.txt</code> file that contains less serious messages.
<p />
See <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.TWikiPatches" title="'Codev.TWikiPatches' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.TWikiPatches</a> in case there are patches (i.e. specific code changes) for particular problems that may affect you (e.g. <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ChangePasswordOnWin2K" title="'Codev.ChangePasswordOnWin2K' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ChangePasswordOnWin2K</a>).
<p />
If you find that the Index feature doesn't work, or topic name searches fail, you should check you have set <code>$egrepCmd</code> and <code>$fgrepCmd</code> correctly, as mentioned above.
<p />
<h3><a name="Permissions"> Permissions </a></h3>
<p />
<a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CygWin" title="'Codev.CygWin' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CygWin</a> has several models for how it does security:
<p />
<ul>
<li> By default, it only implements the Unix 'write' and 'execute' permissions bits - the former is controlled by the Windows Read-Only attribute, while the latter is automatically assigned to files named *.exe or *.com, and to files whose first line is a shebang (i.e. <code>#!/bin/something</code>).  This is what has been used for this cookbook.
</li>
<li> You can enable the 'ntea' or 'ntsec' models, which will increase security but are also likely to introduce permission problems.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
I have not had any problems with TWiki permissions on Windows, unlike Linux/Unix, which is probably because I'm using the default security model for Cygwin.  If you use the other models, you may still be OK if you have local admin rights, and Apache is running as the SYSTEM user (which it uses if started as a service).  If you do have trouble in this area, see the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a>'s advice, some of which will apply to <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.CygWin" title="'Codev.CygWin' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.CygWin</a>, and log any issues in <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments" title="'Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.WindowsInstallCookbookComments</a>.
<p />
<h2><a name="Next_Steps"> Next Steps </a></h2>
<p />
See the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a> for other setup. In particular, you'll probably want to refer to the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide#Enabling_Authentication_of_Users">section on basic authentication</a> - remember to use <code>c:/twiki</code> type filenames (i.e. Windows format) since you are using Apache for Windows.  
<p />
<h3><a name="Improved_authentication"> Improved authentication  </a></h3>
<p />
You may want to investigate <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.WindowsInstallModNTLM" title="'Codev.WindowsInstallModNTLM' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.WindowsInstallModNTLM</a>, which describes how to add an Apache module so that <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.InternetExplorer" title="'Codev.InternetExplorer' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.InternetExplorer</a> users are automatically authenticated based on their Windows domain login - this avoids <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.GettingTheUsernameWrong" title="'Codev.GettingTheUsernameWrong' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.GettingTheUsernameWrong</a> and <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ForgettingPasswords" title="'Codev.ForgettingPasswords' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ForgettingPasswords</a>, which are usually very common among TWiki users.
<p />
<h3><a name="Improved_performance"> Improved performance </a></h3>
<p />
See <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.WindowsModPerlInstallCookbook" title="'Codev.WindowsModPerlInstallCookbook' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.WindowsModPerlInstallCookbook</a> and <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ModPerl" title="'Codev.ModPerl' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ModPerl</a> for information on installing TWiki under Apache's <code>mod_perl</code> - this is somewhat more complex and follows a different model, so it's best to get some experience with TWiki, Apache and Perl first.
<p />
<h2><a name="Format_of_filenames"> Format of filenames </a></h2>
<p />
In your TWiki on Windows installation, it's worth remembering that:
<p />
<ul>
<li> Apache configuration files (e.g. the <code><b>.htaccess</b></code> file and <code><b>c:/apache/conf/httpd.conf</b></code>) always use Windows format paths, with forward slashes, e.g. <code><b>c:/twiki</b></code>
</li>
<li> The same is true for the first line of the TWiki Perl scripts (since this line is interpreted by Apache), e.g. <code><b>c:/cygwin/bin/perl</b></code>
</li>
<li> All other lines in the Perl scripts use Unix format paths, e.g. <code><b>/twiki</b></code> (using Cygwin Perl as per this cookbook)
<ul>
<li> If you are using <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActivePerl" title="'Codev.ActivePerl' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActivePerl</a>, that will use Windows format paths, e.g. <code><b>c:/twiki</b></code>   
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Depending on the Perl version used (Cygwin or <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev.ActivePerl" title="'Codev.ActivePerl' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev.ActivePerl</a>), the TWiki.cfg file uses a mixture of Unix and Cygwin format paths - stick to the format used in the installation step for TWiki.cfg
</li>
<li> RCS always uses Unix format paths, e.g. <code><b>/twiki</b></code>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<p />

<p />
<h1><a name="TWiki_Upgrade_Guide"> TWiki Upgrade Guide </a></h1>
<p />
<em>Upgrade from the previous TWiki 01-Dec-2001 production release to TWiki 01-Feb-2003</em>
<p />
<h2><a name="Overview"> Overview </a></h2>
<p />
This guide describes how to upgrade from TWiki 01-Dec-2001 to TWiki 01-Feb-2003. The new version involves several new features and numerous enhancements to the previous version.
<p />
<h2><a name="Upgrade_Requirements"> Upgrade Requirements </a></h2>
<p />
<ul>
<li> To upgrade from a 01-Dec-2001 standard installation to the latest 01-Feb-2003 TWiki Production Release, follow the instructions below.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong><em>NOTE:</em></strong> To upgrade from a <strong>pre-01-Dec-2001</strong> TWiki, start with   <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiUpgradeTo01Dec2001">TWikiUpgradeTo01Dec2001</a>.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> To upgrade from a Beta of the new release, or if you made custom modifications to the application, read through all new reference documentation, then use the procedure below as a guideline.  
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<h2><a name="Major_Changes_from_TWiki_01_Dec_"> Major Changes from TWiki 01-Dec-2001 </a></h2>
<p />
<ul>
<li> Form and script to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/ManagingWebs">create new webs</a>
</li>
<li> Enhanced Plugin API to manipulate topic data with new functions in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiFuncModule">TWikiFuncModule</a>: <code>readTopicText</code>, <code>saveTopicText</code>, <code>setTopicEditLock</code>, <code>checkTopicEditLock</code>
</li>
<li> New Plugin hooks <code>registrationHandler</code>, <code>beforeEditHandler</code>, <code>afterEditHandler</code>, <code>beforeSaveHandler</code>, <code>writeHeaderHandler</code>, <code>redirectCgiQueryHandler</code>, <code>getSessionValueHandler</code>, <code>setSessionValueHandler</code>
</li>
<li> Internationalization ('I18N') support 8-bit character sets in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiWord">WikiWords</a>, such as ISO-8859-15, KOI8-R
</li>
<li> Possible to omit e-mail address in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebNotify">WebNotify</a>, in which case the e-mail is taken from the user's home page; if the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiName">WikiName</a> is a group name, a notification is sent to all members of the group
</li>
<li> New data storage framework that lets you use external RCS commands for revision control, or a new native Perl implementation that does not depend on the external RCS commands (not recommended yet for production use, see <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev/RcsLite" title="'Codev/RcsLite' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev/RcsLite</a>)
</li>
<li> New AND search; with regular expression enabled, use the semicolon ";" as the AND operator in <code>%SEARCH{}%</code> variable, <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/FormattedSearch">FormattedSearch</a> and <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebSearch">WebSearch</a>
</li>
<li> Many more enhancements, see the complete change log at <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiHistory">TWikiHistory</a>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<h2><a name="Upgrade_Procedure_from_01_Dec_20"> Upgrade Procedure from 01-Dec-2001 to 01-Feb-2003 Release </a></h2>
<p />
The following steps describe the upgrade assuming that <code>$TWIKIROOT</code> is the root of your current 01-Dec-2001 release.  As written this will require some downtime.  A process for switching over without downtime is described at the end of this section.
<p />
<ol>
<li> <strong>Back up and prepare</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Back up all existing TWiki directories <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/pub</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/data</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/templates</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib</code>.
</li>
<li> Create a temporary directory and unpack the ZIP file there.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update files in TWiki root</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Overwrite all <code>*.html</code> and <code>*.txt</code> files in <code>$TWIKIROOT</code> with the new ones.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update template files</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Overwrite all template files in <code>$TWIKIROOT/templates</code> with the new ones.
<ul>
<li> If you have customized your templates, make sure to merge those changes to the new files.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> If you have customized skins or loaded new skins, make sure to merge or apply those changes to the new files.
</li>
<li> Specific changes to templates and skins:
<ul>
<li> Replace <code>%WIKIHOMEURL%</code> with <code>%WIKILOGOURL%</code>
</li>
<li> Replace img tag's <code>src=%PUBURLPATH%/wikiHome.gif</code> with <code>src=%WIKILOGOIMG%</code>
</li>
<li> Replace img tag's <code>alt="TWiki Home"</code> with <code>alt="%WIKILOGOALT%"</code>
</li>
<li> Replace meta tag's <code>charset=iso-8859-1"</code> with <code>charset=ISO-8859-1"</code>
</li>
<li> Add <code>%TOPIC%</code> to form action of <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/GoBox">GoBox</a>
</li>
<li> For internationalized sites, URL encode webs and topics in all form actions, e.g. replace <code>.../view%SCRIPTSUFFIX%/%WEB%/%TOPIC%"</code> with <code>.../view%SCRIPTSUFFIX%/%INTURLENCODE{"%WEB%/%TOPIC%"}%</code>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update script files</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Overwrite all script files in <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin</code> with the new ones.
<ul>
<li> If necessary, change the script names to include the required extension, e.g. <code>.cgi</code>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Edit <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin/setlib.cfg</code> and point <code>$twikiLibPath</code> to the absolute file path of <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib</code> 
</li>
<li> Edit <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin/.htaccess</code> to include a directive for the new <code>manage</code> script:<br />
        <code>&lt;Files "manage"&gt;</code> <br />
        <code>&nbsp; &nbsp; require valid-user</code> <br />
        <code>&lt;/Files&gt;</code>
</li>
<li> Pay attention to the file and directory permissions, the scripts need to be executable, e.g. <code>chmod 775 $TWIKIROOT/bin/*</code>
</li>
<li> If on Non-Unix host, make sure the correct path to the perl interpreter is changed in the first line of every script file. See also <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WindowsInstallCookbook#Editing_the_CGI_scripts">WindowsInstallCookbook</a>.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update library files</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Overwrite the <code>TWiki.cfg</code> configuration file in <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib</code> with the new one.
</li>
<li> Restore the configuration values from the backup. You typically need to configure just the ones in the section "variables that need to be changed when installing on a new server".
</li>
<li> Overwrite the <code>TWiki.pm</code> library in <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib</code> with the new one.
</li>
<li> Copy and overwrite all subdirectories below <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib</code> with the new ones. Make sure to preserve any extra Plugins you might have in <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib/TWiki/Plugins</code> 
</li>
<li> Pay attention to the file and directory permissions, the library files should not be executable, e.g. <code>chmod -R 664 $TWIKIROOT/lib/*</code>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update data files</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Run the <code>bin/testenv</code> script from the browser (e.g. <code>http://localhost/bin/testenv</code>) to verify if the cgi-scripts are running as user <code>nobody</code>.
<ul>
<li> In case not: The <code>*,v</code> RCS repository files delivered with the installation package are locked by user <code>nobody</code> and need to be changed to the user of your cgi-scripts, e.g. <code>www-data</code>:
</li>
<li> Change the lock user in the temporary <code>twiki/data/*</code> directories where you unzipped the installation package: A simple way to switch the locker of the RCS files is to use sed in the :
           <br /> <code>for f in *,v; do sed 's/nobody\:/www-data\:/' $f &gt; x; mv x $f; done</code>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> In the temporary <code>twiki/data/TWiki</code> directory where you unzipped the installation package:
<ul>
<li> Remove the files you do <strong>not</strong> want to upgrade: <code>InterWikis.*</code>, <code>TWikiRegistration.*</code>, <code>TWikiRegistrationPub.*</code>, <code>WebNotify.*</code>, <code>WebPreferences.*</code>, <code>WebStatistics.*</code> and all <code>WebTopic*</code> files.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Rename in the temporary directory the file <code>$TWIKIROOT/data/TWiki/TWikiPreferences.*</code> to <code>TWikiPreferencesSave.*</code>.
</li>
<li> Move all remaining <code>*.txt</code> and <code>*.txt,v</code> files from the temporary <code>data/TWiki</code> directory to your <code>$TWIKIROOT/data/TWiki</code> directory, overwriting the existing ones.
</li>
<li> Merge your original <code>TWikiPreferencesSave.txt</code> settings into <code>$TWIKIROOT/data/TWiki/TWikiPreferences.txt</code>.
</li>
<li> Move the <code>data/_default</code> directory from the temporary location to your <code>$TWIKIROOT/data</code> directory.
</li>
<li> Move the <code>data/Sandbox</code> directory from the temporary location to your <code>$TWIKIROOT/data</code> directory <br /> (The <strong>Test</strong> web has been renamed to <strong>Sandbox</strong> in this release.)
<ul>
<li> There are now <strong>two webs in parallel</strong> (Test and Sandbox) for the purpose of testing (experimenting) TWiki. <br /> Move all relevant topics from Test web to Sandbox web, or motivate the users to do.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Make sure that the directories and files below <code>$TWIKIROOT/data</code> are writable by your cgi-script user.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Adapt the other webs (all other than <code>TWiki</code> and <code>_default</code>)</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Merge the new files <code>WebHome.txt</code> and <code>WebPreferences.txt</code> of your other webs to make sure, you have the improvements applied also in your other webs.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update pub files</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Move all subdirectories below <code>pub/TWiki</code> from your temporary directory into your <code>$TWIKIROOT/pub/TWiki</code> directory.
</li>
<li> Make sure that the directories and files below <code>$TWIKIROOT/pub/TWiki</code> are writable by your cgi-script user.
</li>
<li> Move all files in <code>pub/icn</code> directory from the temporary location to your <code>$TWIKIROOT/pub/icn</code> directory.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Update <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a> to authorize users to create webs</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Add <code>ALLOWWEBMANAGE</code> to the <code>FINALPREFERENCES</code> list so that nobody can overwrite the setting:
<ul>
<li>  Set FINALPREFERENCES = WIKIWEBMASTER, PREVIEWBGIMAGE, SMTPMAILHOST, SMTPSENDERHOST, ALLOWWEBMANAGE
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> Set users or groups allowed to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/ManagingWebs">create new webs</a>: 
<ul>
<li> Set ALLOWWEBMANAGE = <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiAdminGroup">TWikiAdminGroup</a>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li> <strong>Verify installation</strong>:
<ul>
<li> Execute the <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin/testenv</code> script from your browser (e.g. <code>http://localhost/bin/testenv</code>) to see if it reports any issues; fix any potential problems.
</li>
<li> Test your updated TWiki installation to see if you can view, create, edit and rename topics; upload and move attachments; register users.
</li>
<li> Test if the installed Plugins work as expected. You should see the list of installed Plugins in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TextFormattingRules">TextFormattingRules</a>.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<p />
<strong>Note:</strong> These steps assume a downtime during the time of upgrade. You could install the new version in parallel to the existing one and switch over in an instant without affecting the users. As a guideline, install the new version into <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin1</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib1</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/templates1</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/data/TWiki1</code> (from <code>data/TWiki</code>), <code>$TWIKIROOT/pub/TWiki1</code> (from <code>pub/TWiki</code>), and configure <code>TWiki.cfg</code> to point to the same data and pub directory like the existing installation. Once tested and ready to go, reconfigure <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin1/setlib.cfg</code> and <code>$TWIKIROOT/lib1/TWiki.cfg</code>, then rename <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin</code> to <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin2</code>, <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin1</code> to <code>$TWIKIROOT/bin</code>. Do the same with the <code>lib</code>, <code>templates</code> and <code>data/TWiki</code> directories.
<p />
<h2><a name="Known_Issues"> Known Issues </a></h2>
<p />
<ul>
<li> Check <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/Codev/KnownIssuesOfTWiki01Feb2003" title="'Codev/KnownIssuesOfTWiki01Feb2003' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:Codev/KnownIssuesOfTWiki01Feb2003</a> for known issues of TWiki 01-Feb-2003 production release
</li>
</ul>

-- <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> - 01 Feb 2002 <br />

<p />
<h1><a name="TWiki_User_Authentication"> TWiki User Authentication </a></h1>
<p />
<em>TWiki site access control and user activity tracking options</em>
<p />
TWiki does not authenticate users internally, it depends on the <code>REMOTE_USER</code> environment variable. This variable is set when you enable Basic Authentication (.htaccess) or SSL "secure server" authentication (https protocol).
<p />
TWiki uses visitor identification to keep track of who made changes to topics at what time and to manage a wide range of personal site settings. This gives a complete audit trail of changes and activity.
<p />
<h2><a name="Authentication_Options"> Authentication Options </a></h2>
<p />
No special installation steps are required if the server is already authenticated. If it isn't, you have three standard options for controlling user access:
<ol>
<li> <strong>Forget about authentication</strong> to make your site completely public - anyone can browse and edit freely, in classic Wiki mode. All visitors are assigned the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiGuest">TWikiGuest</a> default identity, so you can't track individual user activity. <br />
</li>
<li> <strong>Use SSL (Secure Sockets Layer; HTTPS)</strong> to authenticate and secure the whole server. <br />
</li>
<li> <strong>Use Basic Authentication (.htaccess)</strong> to control access by protecting key scripts: <code>attach</code>, <code>edit=</code>, <code>installpasswd</code>, <code>preview</code>, <code>rename</code>, <code>save</code>, <code>upload</code> using the <code><b>.htaccess file</b></code>. The <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a> has step-by-step instructions. 
</li>
</ol>
<p />
<h3><a name="Partial_Authentication"> Partial Authentication </a></h3>
<p />
<strong>Tracking by IP address</strong> is an experimental feature, enabled in <code>lib/TWiki.cfg</code>. It lets you combine open access to some functions, with authentication on others, with full user activity tracking:
<p />
<ul>
<li> Normally, the <code><b>REMOTE_USER</b></code> environment variable is set for the scripts that are under authentication. If, for example, the <code><b>edit</b></code>, <code><b>save</b></code> and <code><b>preview</b></code> scripts are authenticated, but not <code><b>view</b></code>, you would get your <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiName">WikiName</a> in <code><b>preview</b></code> for the <code><b>%WIKIUSERNAME%</b></code> variable, but <code><b>view</b></code> will show <code><b>TWikiGuest</b></code> instead of your WikiName.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> TWiki can be configured to remember the IP address/username pair whenever an authentication happens (edit topic, attach file). Once remembered, the non-authenticated scripts, like <code><b>view</b></code>, will show the correct username instead of <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiGuest">TWikiGuest</a>.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> Enable this feature by setting the <code><b>$doRememberRemoteUser</b></code> flag in <code>TWiki.cfg</code>. TWiki then persistently stores the IP address/username pairs in the file, <code>$remoteUserFilename</code>, which is <code>"$dataDir/remoteusers.txt"</code> by default.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> <img src="http://192.168.1.49/twiki/pub/TWiki/TWikiDocGraphics/warning.gif" border="0" alt="ALERT!" width="16" height="16" /> This approach can fail if the IP address changes due to dynamically assigned IP addresses or proxy servers. 
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<strong>Quick Authentication Test</strong> - Use the %WIKIUSERNAME% variable to return your current identity:
<p />
<ul>
<li> You are <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiGuest">TWikiGuest</a> 
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<h2><a name="TWiki_Username_vs_Login_Username"> TWiki Username vs. Login Username </a></h2>
<p />
This section applies only if your TWiki site is installed on a server that is both <strong>authenticated</strong> and on an <strong>intranet</strong>.
<p />
TWiki internally manages two usernames: Login Username and TWiki Username.
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong>Login Username:</strong> When you login to the intranet, you use your existing login username, ex: <code><b>pthoeny</b></code>. This name is normally passed to TWiki by the <code><b>REMOTE_USER</b></code> environment variable, and used internally. Login Usernames are maintained by your system administrator.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<ul>
<li> <strong>TWiki Username:</strong> Your name in <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiNotation">WikiNotation</a>, ex: <code><b>PeterThoeny</b></code>, is recorded when you register using <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a>; doing so also generates a personal home page in the Main web.
</li>
</ul>
<p />
TWiki can automatically map an Intranet (Login) Username to a TWiki Username, provided that the username pair exists in the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiUsers">TWikiUsers</a> topic. This is also handled automatically when you register.
<p />
<ul>
<li> <img src="http://192.168.1.49/twiki/pub/TWiki/TWikiDocGraphics/warning.gif" border="0" alt="ALERT!" width="16" height="16" /> In the original TWiki distribution, in <code><b>twiki/data</b></code>, there are two registration form topics, <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a> and <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistrationPub">TWikiRegistrationPub</a>. The original form includes an intranet Login Username field. For Basic Authentication, the original form is replaced by the Pub version. If you started using TWiki on Basic Authentication and want to change, you have to switch back forms for future use, and manually correct the existing entries, by editing <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/TWikiUsers">TWikiUsers</a>, adding the Login Username for each member - <code>PeterThoeny - pthoeny - 01 Jan 1999</code> -  and also in the <code><b>.htpasswd</b></code> file, where you can either replace the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiName">WikiNames</a> or duplicate the entries and have both, so both usernames will work. <strong><em>verification and clearer rewrite to follow in a bit. also link to original installation mention.</em></strong>
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<blockquote>
<strong><em>NOTE:</em></strong> <strong>To correctly enter a <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WikiName">WikiName</a></strong> - your own or someone else's - be sure to include the Main web name in front of the Wiki username, followed by a period, and no spaces. Ex:
<div align="center"> <code><b>Main.WikiUsername</b></code> or <code><b>%MAINWEB%.WikiUsername</b></code> </div>
This points <code><b>WikiUser</b></code> to the TWiki.Main web, where user registration pages are stored, no matter which web it's entered in. Without the web prefix, the name appears as a <span style='background : #FFFFCE;'><font color="#0000FF">NewTopic</font></span><a href="/twiki/bin/edit/TWiki/NewTopic?topicparent=TWiki.TWikiDocumentation">?</a> everywhere but in the Main web.
</blockquote>
<p />
<a name="ChangingPasswords"></a>

<p />
Change and reset passwords using forms on regular pages. Use <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiAccessControl">TWikiAccessControl</a> to restrict use as required.
<p />
<ul>
<li> The <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/ChangePassword">ChangePassword</a> form ( <code><b>TWiki/ChangePassword</b></code> ):
</li>
</ul>
<p />
<blockquote style="background-color:#f5f5f5">
<font size="+2">Change password</font> <br>
<p />
<strong><em>Forgot your old password?</em></strong> Then use <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/ResetPassword">ResetPassword</a> instead. Please only use ResetPassword in case you really forgot your password. Thank you.
<p />
